English translation:

тАЬI solicit understanding from Sadasaspati (= Agni, protector of the assembly), the wonderful, the friend of Indra, the desirable, the bountiful.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The Lord of the Seat, infallible, dear and desirable to Indra,
I have besought for wisdom as our gain.

Jamison Brereton Notes

ay─Бsiс╣гam: I take this form to the root тИЪy─Б тАШbeseech, imploreтАЩ, not to тИЪy─Б тАШdrive, goтАЩ, which does, admittedly, have a well-attested -siс╣г-aorist. So also Witzel Got┼Н, though other translators (including Schmidt, Bс╣Ыhaspati und Indra) render as a verb of motion (Geldner тАЬhabe ich тАж angegangenтАЭ). That interpretation isnтАЩt impossible, but тАШbeseechтАЩ fits the context better.

рд╕рдореБрджреНрд░-рд╢рдмреНрджреЛрд╜рдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЛрджрдзреНрдпреЛрдГ рд╕рд╛рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдЗрддреНрдпреН рдЕрднрд┐рдорддрд╛рд░реНрдерд╕реНрдп рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдирд╛рдпрд╛рд░реНрдгрд╡рд╢рдмреНрджреЗрди рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖реНрдпрддреЗред
рдЕрд░реНрдгрд╕рдГ рд╕рд▓реЛрдкрд╢реНрдЪред рдХрд╛. рел-реи-резрежреп-рейред рдЗрддрд┐ рдорддреНрд╡рд░реНрдереАрдпреЛ рд╡рдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ рд╕рд▓реЛрдкрд╢реНрдЪреерезрее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTruth (of thought) and truthfulness (of speech) were born of arduous penance, thence was nightgenerated, thence also the watery ocean.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Penance: an allusion to the penance of Brahm─Б preceding creation;

Tataс╕е = from that penance, or from him (Brahm─Б); watery ocean: samudra = firmament and ocean (arс╣Зava)

Jamison Brereton

Both truth and reality were born from heat when it was kindled.
From that, night was born, and from that the undulating sea.

Griffith

FROM Fervour kindled to its height Eternal Law and Truth were born:
Thence was the Night produced, and thence the billowy flood of sea arose.

Geldner

Gesetz und Wahrheit wurden aus dem entbrannten Tapas geboren. Daraus entstand die Nacht, daraus der flutende Ozean.

Grassmann

Genaht ist dieser bunte Stier; zum Vater und zur Mutter hat Er sich gesetzt beim Himmelsgang.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬFrom the watery ocean was the year afterwards produced, ordaining nights and days, the ruler ofevery moment.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

From the undulating sea was born the year,
which distributes the days and nights and exerts its will over everyone who blinks [=mortals].

Griffith

From that same billowy flood of sea the Year was afterwards produced,

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe ocean, the royal (Soma), genitive rating progeny in the outstretched (firmament, the) supporter of the water traverses the universe; the showerer (of benefits), the brilliant Soma when effused increases abundantly in the elevated woollen filter.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

As the sea he has roared at his first expansion, begetting the creatures as king of creation.
The bull in the filter, on the sheepтАЩs back, Soma has grown loftily, the drop being pressed.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The verb v─Бvс╣Ыdhe in d concatenates with vardhit─Б╠Бv├бrdhanaс╕е in 39a.

GeldnerтАЩs tr. of p─Бda a, тАЬDer Ocean hat gebr├╝llt bei seiner ersten Ausbreitung,тАЭ seems to imply (though this is not a necessary interpr. of his tr.) that the samudr├б- is a different entity from Soma himself, and his cited IX.107.23 tv├бс╣Г samudr├бm pratham├│ v├н dh─Бrayaс╕е тАЬYou were [/are] the first to to spread out the seaтАЭ (with both samudr├б- and v├н тИЪdhс╣Ы) certainly depicts them as separate. However, IX.86.29 tv├бс╣Г samudr├│ asi тАж, t├бvem─Б╠Бс╕е p├б├▒ca prad├н┼Ыo v├нdharmaс╣Зi тАЬYou are the sea, тАж; yours are these five regions in your [/their] expansionтАЭ (also with samudr├б- and the -n-stem loc. v├нdharman/-с╣Зi as here) asserts the identity of Soma and the samudr├б-. Since forms of тИЪkrand тАШroarтАЩ in IX (like ├бkr─Бn here) have Soma as their subject (incl. in vss. 13, 18, 28, 32, 33 in this hymn), the identification of Soma and the sea seems assured here.

In the first vault of heaven loud roared the Ocean, King of all being, generating creatures.
Steer, in the filter, on the fleecy summit, Soma, the Drop effused, hath waxen mighty.

рддрдерд╛ рд╡рд┐рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдореЗрдзрд╛рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рдореНрдордзреНрдпреЗ рдЛрд╖рд┐рд░реНрднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рдпрдГ рдкрд░реЛрдХреНрд╖рдореНрдкрд╢реНрдпрддрд┐ рд╕рдЛрд╖рд┐рдГ ред рдЛрд╖рд┐рд░реНрджрд░реНрд╢- рдирд╛рджрд┐рддрд┐ ред рдореГрдЧрд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдорд╣рд┐рд╖реЛрднрд╡рддрд┐ рдорд╣рд┐рд╖рд╛рдЦреНрдпреЛрдмрд▓рд╡рд╛рдиреН рд░рд╛рдЬрд╛рднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рддрдерд╛ рдЧреГрдзреНрд░рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд┐- рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рдгрд╛рдВ рд╢реНрдпреЗрдирдГ рд╢рдВрд╕рдиреАрдпрдГ рдкрдХреНрд╖рд┐рд░рд╛рдЬреЛрднрд╡рддрд┐ ред рд╡рдирд╛рдирд╛рдВ рд╡рдирддрд┐рд░реНрд╣рд┐рд╕рд╛рдХрд░реНрдорд╛ ред рд╣рд┐рдВрд╕рдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЫреЗрджрдХрд╛- рдирд╛рдореНрдордзреНрдпреЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрд┐рддрд┐рдГ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХрдГ рдЫреЗрджрдХреЛрд╕рд┐ ред рдПрд╡рдореНрдкреНрд░рднрд╛рд╡рдГ рд╕реЛрдордГ рд░реЗрднрдиреН рд╢рдмреНрджрд╛рдпрдорд╛рдирдГрд╕рдиреН рдкрд╡рд┐ рддреНрд░рдореВрд░реНрдгрд╛рд╕реНрддреБрдХреЗрди рдХреГрддрдорддреНрдпреЗрддрд┐ рдЕрддрд┐рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рее рем рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Brahm─Б of the gods, the guide of the sages, the с╣Ыс╣гi of the pious, the buffalo of wild animals, the falcon of the vultures, the hatchet of deadly weapons, the Soma passes through the filter with a roar.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Brahm─Б of the gods: i.e., the king of the gods; or, it may mean the br─Бhmaс╣Зa of the priests; the с╣Ыс╣гi: yaс╕е parokс╣гam pa┼Ыyati sa с╣Ыс╣гiс╕е, с╣Ыsirdar┼Ыan─Бt (Nirukta 2.11)

Jamison Brereton

Formulator for the gods, trail-blazer for the sage poets, seer for the inspired poets, buffalo of the wild beasts,
falcon of the birds of prey, axe of the treesтАФSoma goes rasping
through the filter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though the syntax is kept absolutely constant - nom. sg. + gen. pl. - there is a shifting functional relationship between the head noun and its genitive in the seven phrases here: the first two are roles Soma performs for the group identified by the gen., the next three a particular, and superior, individual token from the group (though the third pairing, тАЬseer for/of the inspired poets,тАЭ is ambiguous between the first type and the second), and the last is sort of a negative version of the role he plays for the group.

Griffith

Brahman of Gods, the Leader of the poets, Rsi of sages, Bull of savage creatures,
Falcon amid the vultures, Axe of forests, over the cleansing sieve goes Soma singing.

Geldner

Der Hohepriester der G├╢tter, der Pfadfinder der Seher, der Rishi unter den Beredten, der B├╝ffel unter den wilden Tieren, der Adler unter den Geiern, die Axt f├╝r die B├дume, geht Soma laut redend durch die Seihe.

Grassmann

Der G├╢tter Beter und der Priester F├╝hrer, der S├дnger Dichter und der Stier der Thiere, Der Geier Adler und die Axt der W├дlder, der Soma wandert singend durch die Seihe.

Keith

I The gander seated in purity, the bright one seated in the atmosphere,
The Hotr seated at the altar, the guest seated in the house,
Seated among men, seated in the highest, seated in holy order, seated in the firmament, Born of the waters, born of the cows, born of holy order, born of the mountain, the great holy order.

тАЬGrant us today, divine Savit─Б affluence with progeny, and drive away evil dreams.тАЭ

English translation:

тАЬRemove from us, divine Savit─Б, all misfortunes; bestow upon us that which is good,тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bhadram = progeny, cattle, dwelling, praj─Б vai bhadram, pasa‘vo bhadram, gс╣Ыham bhadram iti

All difficulties impel away, god Savitar.
What is beneficial, that impel here to us.

Savitar, God, send far away all sorrows and calamities,
And send us only what is good.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬFour are his horns; three are his feet; his heads are two, his hands are seven; the triple-bound showerer (of benefits) roars aloud; the mighty deity has entered among men.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This verse is preferentially applied to Agni, identified either with yaj├▒a or with ─Аditya; the four horns of the yaj├▒a are the four vedas; of ─Аditya, the four cardinal points of the horizon; the three feet of yaj├▒a are the three daily sacrifices; of ─Аditya, morning, noon, evening; the two heads of yaj├▒a are two particular ceremonies termed brahmaudanam and pravargya; of ─Аditya, day and night; the seven hands of yaj├▒a are the seven metres; of ─Аditya, the seven rays, or the six seasons and their aggregate, or the year, the seventh; the term vс╣Ыс╣гabha phal─Бn─Бm vaс╣Ыsit─Б, the rainer of rewards, applies to yaj├▒a and ─Аditya; so does roraite, he roars, implying the noise made by the repetition of the mantras of the vedas; the three bonds of yaj├▒a are: mantra, kalpa and br─Бhmaс╣Зa, the prayer, the ceremonial; the rationale of ─Аditya, the three regions, earth, mid-air and heaven; another view is to limit vс╣Ыс╣гabha k─Бm─Бnam varс╣гit─Б to yaj├▒a; the four horns are the priests: the hot─Б, udg─Бt─Б, adhvaryu and brahm─Б; the three feet are the three vedas; the two heads the havirdh─Бna and pravargya rites; the hands are the seven priests, or seven metres; the three bonds the three daily sacrifices; Nirukta 13.7 applies the verse to yaj├▒a

Jamison Brereton

Four are his horns, three his feet; two heads, seven hands are his. Triply bound, the bull keeps on roaring. The great god has entered mortals.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Clearly no bull found in nature. The numerology here presumably has to do with items in the ritual. For a conspectus of later interpr., see Witzel Got┼Н n.

Griffith

Four are his horns, three are the feet that bear him; his heads are two, his hands are seven in number.
Bound with a triple bond the Steer roars loudly: the mighty God hath entered in to mortals.

Geldner

Vier H├╢rner, drei F├╝├Яe hat er, zwei K├╢pfe, sieben H├дnde hat er. Dreifach gefesselt br├╝llt der Stier. Der gro├Яe Gott ist in die Sterblichen eingegangen.

Grassmann

Vier H├╢rner hat er, auf drei F├╝ssen steht er, zwei K├╢pfe sind ihm und der H├дnde sieben-, Dreifach gebunden br├╝llt der Stier gewaltig, der grosse Gott begab sich zu den Menschen.

рд╕рд╛рдпрдг-рднрд╛рд╖реНрдпрдореН

рдкрдгрд┐рднрд┐рдГ рдЕрд╕реБрд░реИрдГ рдЧрд╡рд┐ рдЧреЛрд╖реБ рддреНрд░рд┐рдзрд╛ рдХреНрд╖реАрд░рджрдзреНрдпрд╛рдЬреНрдпрднреЗрджреЗрди рддреНрд░рд┐рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░рдВ рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдирд┐рд╣рд┐рддрдВ рдЧреБрд╣реНрдпрдорд╛рдирдВ рдЧреЛрдкрд┐рддрдВ рдШреГрддрдВ рджреАрдкреНрддрдВ рд░рд╕рд░реВрдкрдВ рд╡рд╛ рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпрдВ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рд╕рдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рдЕрдиреНрд╡рд╡рд┐рдиреНрджрдиреН рдЕрд▓рднрдиреНрдд ред рддрддреНрд░ рдЗрдиреНрджреНрд░ рдПрдХрдВ рдХреНрд╖реАрд░рдВ рдЬрдЬрд╛рди рдЙрджрдкрд╛рджрдпрддреН ред рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдПрдХрдВ рдЬрдЬрд╛рди ред рд╡реЗрдирд╛рддреН рдХрд╛рдиреНрддрд┐рдорддрдГ рдЕрдЧреНрдиреЗрд░реНрдЧрдордирд╡рддреЛ рд╡рд╛рдпреЛрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдПрдХрдВ рдШреГрддрдВ рд╕реНрд╡рдзрдпрд╛ рдЕрдиреНрдиреЗрди рдирд┐рдорд┐рддреНрддреЗрди рджреНрд░рд╡реНрдпреЗрдг рд╡рд╛ рд╕рд╛рдзрдиреЗрди рдирд┐рд╖реНрдЯрддрдХреНрд╖реБрдГ рдирд┐рд░рдкрд╛рджрдпрдиреН рджреЗрд╡рд╛рдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gods discovered the Gh─л concealed by the Paс╣Зis, plural ced three-fold in the cow; Indra genitive rated one (portion), S┼лrya another, the (other gods) fabricated one from the resplendent (Agni), for the sake of the oblation.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The paс╣Зis are asuras; the three forms or states in which the gh─л was deposited in the cow were milk, curds and butter, of which Indra engendered jaj─Бna, milk, S┼лrya butter, and the god (dev─Бsaс╕е) fabricated (tatakс╣гuс╕е) curds from the shining, ven─Бt, that is Agni; another rendering is dev─Бsaс╕е dvij─Бtayaс╕е, the twice-born

Jamison Brereton

Triply deposited, being hidden by the niggardsтАФthe gods discovered the ghee in the cow.
Indra begat one; the Sun begat one; from the seeker they fashioned one through their own power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

As was just noted, the Paс╣Зis (niggards) may be indirectly implicated in the verb avam─лt in 2d. Here they appear overtly, as the hiders of ghee – presumably a reference to their stealing of the cows, since the gods find the ghee in the cow in p─Бda b.

The threefold nature and creation of ghee has been variously interpreted; it again participates in the numerology of the hymn. I do not have a view on it.

Griffith

That oil in triple shape the Gods discovered laid down within the Cow, concealed by Panis.
Indra produced one shape, Surya another: by their own power they formed the third from Vena.

Geldner

Dreifach geteilt fanden das von den Pani┬┤s verborgene Ghrita die G├╢tter wieder in der Kuh. Indra hat das eine, Surya das eine erzeugt. Eines haben sie aus dem Seher durch eigene Kraft herausgebildet.

Grassmann

Die dreigetheilt versteckt war von den Pani’s, die Butter fanden in der Kuh die G├╢tter; Die eine zeugte Indra, Surja eine, und eine schufen selbst sie aus Verlangen.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yajus. 3.35;

Pracoday─Бt = who may animate, or enlighten our intellect;

Savit─Б = the soul, as one with the soul of the world, Brahma; when we meditate on the light which is one with Brahma, his own light, which, from its consuming influences on ignorance and its consequences, is termed Bhargas, and is that which is desirable, from its being to be known or worshiped by all (vareс╣Зyam) the property of the supreme being, (parame┼Ыvara), the creator of the world, and the animator, impeller or urger (savit─Б), through the internally abiding spirit (antary─Бm) of all creatures; yaс╕е, although masculine, may be relative to the neuter noun bhargas, that light which animates all (dhiyaс╕е) acts (karm─Бс╣Зi), or illumes all understanding (buddhiс╕е); again, devasya savituс╕е may mean, of the bright or radiant sun, as the progenitor of all, sarvasya prasavitur, and bhargas may be understood as the sphere or orb of light, the consumer of sins, p─Бp─Бn─Бm t─Бpakam tejo maс╣Зс╕Нalam; bhargas may also mean food, and the prayer may only implore the sun to provide sustenance, tasya pras─Бd─Бd ann─Бdi lakс╣гaс╣Зam phalam dh─лmahi tasya ─Бdh─Бrabh┼лta bhavema, we anticipate from his favour the reward that is characterized by food and the like, that is, may we be supported by him

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН - рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

The mantra-s

The S─Бvitr─л is the core mantra used in Savitrup─Бsan─Б. It also has other notable deployments, which will be described later. Its с╣Ыс╣гi is Vi┼Ыv─Бmitra of the clan of G─Бthin, the chandas is nicс╣Ыd g─Бyatr─л and the devat─Б is Savitс╣Ы. It is from the 3_r__d_ maс╣Зс╕Нala of the с╣Ъgveda (RV 3.62.10). The meter is termed nicс╣Ыd g─Бyatr─л because the syllable count is 23, one short of the usual 24 for a g─Бyatr─л. This arises due to the intrinsic saс╣Гdhi, which creates рд╡рд░реЗрдгреНрдпрдореН from рд╡рд░реЗрдгрд┐рдпрдореН . The S─Бvitr─л goes thus:

рддрддреН рд╕реСрд╡рд┐реТрддреБрд░реН рд╡рд░реЗреСрдгреНрдпреТрдореН рднрд░реНрдЧреЛреС рджреЗреТрд╡рд╕реНрдпреС рдзреАрдорд╣рд┐ ред рдзрд┐рдпреЛреТ рдпреЛ рдирдГреС рдкреНрд░рдЪреЛреТрджрдпрд╛реСрддреН рее

Given the popularity of the S─Бvitr─л it is common to see numerous translations of the same; however, these often do not get certain aspects of the Old Vedic register of Sanskrit. It is important that one does the japa of this mantra with a proper grasp of its sense in the original language. Hence, we provide a translation of the mantra in full here.

tat= that; Savituс╕е= of Savit─Б; vareс╣Зyam= excellent or desirable; bhargaс╕е= radiance (neuter accusative); devasya= of the god; dh─лmahi= may we fix [our mind]/ may we focus on; dhiyaс╕е= insights (plural of dh─л); yaс╕е= who; nas= our; pracoday─Бt= may he inspire.

There are a few key points to make note of: first, the verb form dh─лmahi; this is the ─Б┼Ы─лr-liс╣Е (benedictive) 1st person plural form of the root dh─Б, which belongs to class 3 (juhoty─Бdi gaс╣Зa). We are unaware of the occurrence of other ─Б┼Ы─лr-liс╣Е forms of the verb dh─Б in the RV. It is used symmetrically with the 3rd person singular ─Б┼Ы─лr-liс╣Е form of the verb pra-cud i.e. pracoday─Бt. These forms are not commonly used outside of such mantra-s suggesting that it was an ancient usage of a verb-pair presenting a relationship between the worshipers (dh─лmahi) and the god (pracoday─Бt).

Second, the name of the god Savitс╣Ы is commonly combined with the word deva (god). This combination probably again has an ancient connotation, which is reflected in theonyms of other Indo-European branches like proto-Germanic *Tiwaz тЖТ Tyr. It (theos) was probably also used in this sense for the Greek Hyperion1, the likely cognate of Savitс╣Ы, in the Homeric language.

Third, the word dhiyaс╕е, has been specifically chosen for alliteration with dh─лmahi2. It means not just any thought but specifically inspired thought or insight that leads to the тАЬseeingтАЭ of special knowledge, such as that embodied in a Vedic mantra.

Thus, we get,

May we focus on the excellent radiance of the deva Savitс╣Ы who will inspire our insights.

Adjuncts
The S─Бvitr─л is prefixed with the three vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s for the actual japa.

рднреВрд░реН рднреБрд╡рдГ рд╕реБрд╡рдГ ред

The three basic vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s are to understood as the three realms, the earth, the atmosphere and the heavens, which are pervaded by the light of the god Savitс╣Ы. These are given above in the Yajurvedic form, which may also be followed in Atharvavedic tradition. In the с╣Ъgvedic tradition the internal saс╣Гdhi is enacted and we have рд╕реНрд╡рдГ for рд╕реБрд╡рдГ. The mysteries of these vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s are explained, among other places, in the Taittir─лya-┼Ыruti.

For the practice of pr─Бс╣З─Бy─Бma, it is prefixed with the 7 vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s.

реР рднреВрдГ ред реР рднреБрд╡рдГ ред рдУрдЧреНрдБ рд╕реБрд╡рдГ ред реР рдорд╣рдГ ред реР рдЬрдирдГ ред реР рддрдкрдГ ред рдУрдЧреНрдБ рд╕рддреНрдпрдореН ред

These may be understood as a larger set of 7 regions of space, which are pervaded by the light of Savitс╣Ы. The nasals preceding sa are given as per the Yajurvedic tradition. They are rendered as the usual nasals in the RV and AV traditions.

It suffixed by the incantation known as the brahma┼Ыiras.

реР рдЖрдкреЛреТ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддреАреТ рд░рд╕реЛреТ рд╜рдореГрддрдВреТ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдореТ рднреВрд░реН-рднреБрд╡реТ-рд╕реБрд╡реТрд░реЛрейрдореН рее

Here, ─Бpaс╕е= waters; jyotiс╕е= light; rasaс╕е= life fluids; amс╣Ыtaс╣Г= immortality; brahma= mantra-power. bh┼лс╕е, bhuvaс╕е and suvaс╕е and the three main vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s

Then there is the four-footed form which is a mystery teaching in the ┼Ыruti of the ┼Ъukla-yajurvedin-s. This is obtained by adding the below.

рдкреТрд░реЛ-рд░реСрдЬрд╕реЗреТ рд╜рд╕рд╛рд╡реТрджреН рдУрейрдореН рее

This technically converts it into an anuс╣гс╣нubh due the addition of 8 additional syllables. In the mystery teaching it is termed the beautiful or the vivid foot that is beyond the immediate space (rajas: see section below for details). In the same teaching it is revealed that the 4_t__h_ foot is a critical aspect of both abhic─Бrika and vс╣Ыddhi deployments of the S─Бvitr─л. Indeed, combined with the teaching of ┼Ъaunaka it might be deployed along with the S─Бvitr─л with syllables inverted (vipar─лta-prayoga) for abhic─Бrika purposes.

The Atharvan tradition gives a saс╣Гpuс╣нikaraс╣Зa of the S─Бvitr─л known as the Mah─Бs─Бvitr─л. It goes thus:

реР рднреВрдГ ред реР рднреБрд╡рдГ ред реР рд╕реНрд╡рдГ ред реР рдорд╣рдГ ред реР рдЬрдирдГ ред реР рддрдкрдГ ред реР рд╕реТрддреНрдпрдВ ред

рдзрд┐рдпреЛреТ рдпреЛ рдирдГреС рдкреНрд░рдЪреЛреТрджрдпрд╛реСрддреН рее
реР рдЖрдкреЛреТ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддреАреТ рд░рд╕реЛреТ рд╜рдореГрддрдВреТ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдореТ рднреВрд░реН-рднреБрд╡реТ-рд╕реБрд╡реТрд░реЛрейрдореН рее
реР рднреВрд░реН-рднреБрд╡рдГ-рд╕реБрд╡рд░реН-рдорд╣рд░реН-рдЬрдирд╕реН-рддрдкрдГ рд╕рддреНрдпрдВ рдордзреБреС рдХреНрд╖рд░рдиреНрддрд┐ ред
реР рдЖрдкреЛреТ рдЬреНрдпреЛрддреАреТ рд░рд╕реЛреТ рд╜рдореГрддрдВреТ рдмреНрд░рд╣реНрдореТ рднреВрд░реН-рднреБрд╡реТ-рд╕реНрд╡рд░реЛрейрдореН ред
рдУрдореНреС рддрджреН-рдмреНрд░реТрд╣реНрдо ред рдУрдореНреС рддрджреН-рд╡рд╛реТрдпреБрдГ ред рдУрдореНреС рддрджреН-рдЖреТрддреНрдорд╛ ред рдУрдореНреС рддрддреН-рд╕реТрддреНрдпрдореН ред рдУрдореНреС рддрддреН-рд╕рд░реНрд╡рдореНреС ред рдУрдореНреС рддрддреН-рдкреБрд░реЛрдВреТ рдирдордГ рее

Some hold that deploying this form of the mantra 10├Ч can be considered an equivalent of deploying the regular version 108├Ч. This mantra is also seen as a combination of that of the gods Savitс╣Ы and Vayu. These two are an ancient pair as indicated by the Mс╣Ыg─Бra mantra-s. Savitс╣Ы pervades space with light, while the Vayu pervades it as the rarefied substance and the force which holds the celestial bodies together. These two thus form the foundation of existence.

The Atharvan tradition also teaches the mystery deployment, which adds the Atharva┼Ыiras comprised of the Atharvanic high vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s.

реР рднреБрд░реН-рднреБрд╡рдГ-рд╕реНрд╡рдГ ред
реР рддрддреН рд╕реСрд╡рд┐реТрддреБрд░реН рд╡рд░реЗреСрдгреНрдпреТрдореН рднрд░реНрдЧреЛреС рджреЗреТрд╡рд╕реНрдпреС рдзреАрдорд╣рд┐ ред

реР рднреВрд░реН рднреБрд╡рдГ рд╕реНрд╡рд░реН рдЬрдирджреН рд╡реГрдзрддреН рдХрд░рджреН рд░реБрд╣рдиреН рдорд╣рддреН рддрдЪреН рдЫрдореН рдУрдореН рее

Here, the vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s janad, vс╣Ыdhat, karat, ruhat, mahat, tat, ┼Ыam and oс╣Г are the special vy─Бhс╣Ыti-s of the Bhс╣Ыgv─Бс╣Еgiras. These are part of the secret teaching of the Atharvan. The knower of the Bhс╣Ыgv─Бс╣Еgirasa-┼Ыruti may use this deployment to protecting himself while attacking his enemies with the stoma-bh─Бga-prayoga.

The vipar─лta-prayoga (inverse deployment) is specified for abhic─Бrika purposes.

рддреНрдпрд╛рджрдЪреЛрдкреНрд░ рдиреЛ рдпреЛ рдпреЛрдзрд┐ ред

A variant inverse deployment involves merely inverting the three feet.

рдзрд┐рдпреЛреТ рдпреЛ рдирдГреС рдкреНрд░рдЪреЛреТрджрдпрд╛реСрддреН ред рднрд░реНрдЧреЛреС рджреЗреТрд╡рд╕реНрдпреС рдзреАрдорд╣рд┐ ред рддрддреН рд╕реСрд╡рд┐реТрддреБрд░реН рд╡рд░реЗреСрдгрд┐реТрдпреЛрдВ рее

The mysteries

The ┼Ыruti of the the V─Бjasaneyin-s provides a mystery teaching regarding the S─Бvitr─л, which associates the 3 feet of the core mantra with a triad of triads, which is summarized below.

  • рднреВрдорд┐рдГ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖рдореН рджреНрдпреМрд╕реН
  • рдЛрдЪрдГ рдпрдЬреВрдВрд╖рд┐ рд╕рд╛рдорд╛рдирд┐
  • рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрдГ рдЕрдкрд╛рдирдГ рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирдГ

The one who meditates on the S─Бvitr─л with this knowledge is understood as penetrating

  • the realms of the universe with the first triad,
  • the realms of Veda-s with the second triad and
  • realms of life with the the third triad.

The fourth foot is said to blaze beyond the expanse of the visible space, the тАЬrajasтАЭ and its knowledge confers splendor.

The Atharvan tradition holds (the teaching of Maudgalya to Gl─Бva Maitreya) that the S─Бvitr─л is pervaded by the god Deva Savitс╣Ы and his consort S─Бvitr─л in the form of 12 pairs of forms corresponding to each syllable (Figure). In these forms the two deities pervade the universe and the ritual. This presentation in the Atharvan tradition is consistent with the statement of V─Бmadeva Gautama in the RV: рдЖрдкреНрд░рд╛реТ рд░рдЬрд╛рдВреСрд╕рд┐ рджрд┐реТрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдирд┐реТ рдкрд╛рд░реНрдерд┐реСрд╡рд╛реТ in RV 4.53.3, i.e. celestial and the earthly realms. The three feet of the S─Бvitr─л are described giving rise to three sequences of emanations that culminate in the ritual observance of the br─Бhmaс╣Зa (Figure below; lower panel). The ritualist who performs the deployment of the S─Бvitr─л with the appropriate knowledge of the omniform manifestation of Savitс╣Ы and his consort and the emanations of the three feet meets with success.

рдмрд▓реСрдкреНрд░рдордердирд╛рдпреТ рдирдордГреТ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реСрднреВрддрджрдордирд╛рдпреТ рдирдореЛреС
рдореТрдиреЛрдиреНрдореСрдирд╛рдпреТ рдирдордГреС

рдорд╛рдирд╕рддрд░рдЩреНрдЧрд┐рдгреАрдХреГрддреН - рдЯрд┐рдкреНрдкрдиреА

The vAmadeva mantra of the pa~nchabrahma-s is the mantra of the 11 rudra-s. It names a total of 11 rudra-s, an ancient number associated with the rudra-s. The shatapatha brAhmaNa of the shuklayajurveda gives a different list of rudra-s, 9 in number. Notably, this number is important in the later tAntrika tradition (e.g., navAtman bhairava and the navAtman mantra of the early Urdhvasrotas; 9^2 also underlies the structure of the vyomavyApin mantra).

9 female forms of these rudra-s are the 9 shakti-s of the central maNDala of shiva in both the dakShiNasrotas and Urdhvasrotas. They are arranged as an ogdoad in an 8-petalled lotus around sadAshiva or svachChanda-bhairava, with manonmanI as the shakti in the center alongside shiva.+++(4)+++

However, some texts, like the saiddhAntika texts, kiraNa and parAkhya, list 9 rudra-s.
These are extracted from the original 11 of the vAmadeva mantra parallel to the 9 shakti-s of rudra:

  1. vAmadeva; 2. jyeShTha; 3. rudra; 4. kAla; 5. kalavikaraNa (kalAkShepa); 6. balavikaraNa (balakShepa); 7. balapramathana; 8. sarvabhutasdamana; 9. manonmana

The corresponding ┼Ъaktis extracted from this mantra include all but shreSTha and bala, suggesting that the drAviDapATha could be the older one. - GA

The parAkhya tantra, which lists slightly different variants (in brackets) of some of these rudra-s mentions explicitly that they reside with the respective shakti-s.

The sAdhaka of the nine-bIja navAtman invokes the 9 rudra-s on padmapITha-s blossoming in the chidabdhiH.

But analysis of the pa~nchabrahma-s from various sources shows that the vAmadeva yajuSh is polymorphic across different traditions:

The 9-name version:

We believe this variant goes back to the late kR^iShNa-yajurveda itself. Although the bodhAyana-s follow the taittirIya shruti, they have their own mantrapATha and prayoga with variants. They have a rite known as the pa~nchabrahma-nyAsa, which gives the vAmadeva mantra with 9 names:

vAmadevAya namo jyeShThAya namo rudrAya namaH kAlAya namaH kalavikaraNAya namo balavikaraNAya namo balapramathanAya namaH sarvabhUtadamanAya namo manonmanAya namaH ||

The 9 names are used for the rudra-sarvopachAra-pUjA in the bodhAyana payoga.

This 9-name version of the brahma-mantra was inherited by some siddhAnta-tantra-s, e.g., 1. kAlottara, which specifies it for several prayoga-s. 2. nishvAsa-kArika. The system of 9 rudra-s and 9 shakti-s is clearly derived from the bodhAyana variant. The invocation of the rudra-shakti-s specified by the female forms of the alternating names in the mantra is already seen in the bodhAyana prayoga.

The 8-name version:

OM vAmadevAya namo jyeShThAya namo rudrAya namaH kAlAya namaH kalavikaraNAya namo balapramathanAya namaH sarvabhUtadamanAya namo manonmanAya namaH ||

This is specified by the second adhyAya of the pAshupatasUtra-s. Some saiddhAntika-s prescribe this instead of the 9-name version. For example, it is explicitly provided by the deshika-s j~nAnashiva and vimalashiva, and mahArAja bhojadeva paramAra in their respective prayoga manuals.

A corrupt version of the 8-name version is also provided by the pa~ncharAtra vaiShNava sanatkumAra tantra.

The 7-name version:
OM vAmadevAya jyeShThAya namo rudrAya cha namaH | kalavikaraNAya namo balapramathanAya namaH | sarvabhUtadamanAya shrImanonmanAya namaH ||

This version is found in the sanatkumArIya pa~nchabrahma (siddha-shaMkara) tantra. Above is the version in the printed text. Its quasi-metrical variant is seen in a prayoga based on it:

vAmadevAya jyeShThAya namo rudrAya cha namaH |
namaH kalavikaraNAya balapramathanAya |
namaH sarvabhUtadamanAya manonmanAya cha ||

The more common 11, 9, and 8 name variants probably emerged early and existed side by side, depending on the theological principle onto which they were mapped.

рд░реВрдкреЗрднреНрдп рдПрднреНрдпрдГ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрднреНрдпреЛ
рдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рдВ рдХрд░реЛрддреНрдпреН рдЕрдгреБрдГ ред
рдирдорд╕реНрдХрд╛рд░рдГ рдкрд░рд┐рддреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдГ
рдХрд╛рд░реНрдп-рдХрд╛рд░рдг-рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдГ рее”

While the scriptures of pAshupata-s who followed the lakulin are lost, a fragment of their text is preserved by kShemarAja, the cousin of abhinavagupta in his commentary on the svachChanda-tantra. It gives an important insight into how they viewed the rudra of the bahurUpI-R^ik.

The triad of rudra-s, i.e., the aghora-s, ghora-s and ghoraghoratara-s are seen as occupying a tripartite universe with the aghora-s in the upper “ideal” world (starting with vAmeshvara);
the ghora-s constituting a terrible web permeating the material worlds (starting with gopati and culminating in gahana). Finally, the ghoraghoratara rudra-s constitute the substratal world and include the vidyeshvara-s culminating in ananta. It is notable that the vidyeshvara-s form the inner circle in the siddhAnta.

This suggests that it inherited that configuration from a distinct pAshupata predecessor.

This lakulin formulation next mentions the key role of the shakti-s of these rudra-s, who are also understood as the shakti-s of the primary rudra parameshvara himself. The formulation resembles the early trika (pUrvAmnAya)-aligned tantra-s.Thus, the differentiation of the srotAMsi was already underway in the atimArga substratum.

bahurUpI was archaic but popular para-vedic mantra used outside of core saMhitA ritual, likely among the earliest shaiva-s. It was incorporated once, relatively late into the saMhitA of the maitrAyaNIya-s in the context of the raudra shrauta rituals and independently into mahAnArAyaNopaniShat traditions. In that later class of traditions, it was likely an independent transfer from the shaiva traditions (by now early pAshupata). The mantramArga inherited from pAshupata where it was already polymorphic with saiddhAntika-s and dakShiNa-s inheriting alternative variants.

тАЬGrant us today, divine Savit─Б affluence with progeny, and drive away evil dreams.тАЭ

Impel away the bad dream.

English translation:

тАЬRemove from us, divine Savit─Б, all misfortunes; bestow upon us that which is good,тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bhadram = progeny, cattle, dwelling, praj─Б vai bhadram, pasa‘vo bhadram, gс╣Ыham bhadram iti

Jamison Brereton

All difficulties impel away, god Savitar.
What is beneficial, that impel here to us.

Griffith

Savitar, God, send far away all sorrows and calamities,
And send us only what is good.

Geldner

Grassmann

O schaffe alles Ungemach von uns hinweg, Gott Savitar; Was heilsam ist, das schaff uns her.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe Brahm─Б of the gods, the guide of the sages, the с╣Ыс╣гi of the pious, the buffalo of wild animals, the falcon of the vultures, the hatchet of deadly weapons, the Soma passes through the filter with a roar.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The Brahm─Б of the gods: i.e., the king of the gods; or, it may mean the br─Бhmaс╣Зa of the priests; the с╣Ыс╣гi: yaс╕е parokс╣гam pa┼Ыyati sa с╣Ыс╣гiс╕е, с╣Ыsirdar┼Ыan─Бt (Nirukta 2.11)

Jamison Brereton

Formulator for the gods, trail-blazer for the sage poets, seer for the inspired poets, buffalo of the wild beasts,
falcon of the birds of prey, axe of the treesтАФSoma goes rasping
through the filter.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Though the syntax is kept absolutely constant - nom. sg. + gen. pl. - there is a shifting functional relationship between the head noun and its genitive in the seven phrases here: the first two are roles Soma performs for the group identified by the gen., the next three a particular, and superior, individual token from the group (though the third pairing, тАЬseer for/of the inspired poets,тАЭ is ambiguous between the first type and the second), and the last is sort of a negative version of the role he plays for the group.

Griffith

Brahman of Gods, the Leader of the poets, Rsi of sages, Bull of savage creatures,
Falcon amid the vultures, Axe of forests, over the cleansing sieve goes Soma singing.

Geldner

Der Hohepriester der G├╢tter, der Pfadfinder der Seher, der Rishi unter den Beredten, der B├╝ffel unter den wilden Tieren, der Adler unter den Geiern, die Axt f├╝r die B├дume, geht Soma laut redend durch die Seihe.

Grassmann

Der G├╢tter Beter und der Priester F├╝hrer, der S├дnger Dichter und der Stier der Thiere, Der Geier Adler und die Axt der W├дlder, der Soma wandert singend durch die Seihe.

Elizarenkova

Keith

I The gander seated in purity, the bright one seated in the atmosphere,
The Hotr seated at the altar, the guest seated in the house,
Seated among men, seated in the highest, seated in holy order, seated in the firmament, Born of the waters, born of the cows, born of holy order, born of the mountain, the great holy order.
